Objection: The Soul Persists and Can Return to Any Body
The objector argues that the soul is a self-subsistent substance and resurrection is possible by returning it to any body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical objection that the soul is a self-subsistent substance that survives death and can be returned to any body for resurrection, and how this challenges the orthodox view.

Core Idea
The soul, not the body, is the basis of personal identity.

This passage presents the philosopher's objection to the orthodox view of bodily resurrection. He argues that the soul is a lasting substance, supported by scripture, and that resurrection is simply the soul's return to any body, since identity lies in the soul. This sets up the challenge that Ghazali will answer in the following pages.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the objector's use of scriptural evidence.
This is not Ghazali's own view; it is the argument he will refute.
2
Identify the key claim
The objector claims that personal identity rests in the soul, not the body, because the body changes throughout life.
3
Reflect on the challenge
Consider why this argument poses a problem for traditional resurrection: if the soul can return to any body, is it truly the same person?
This will be answered by Ghazali later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض، أن يقال بم تنكرون على من يختار القسم الأخير، ويرى أن النفس باقية بعد الموت، وهى جوهر قائم بنفسه، فإن ذلك لا يخالف الشرع بل دل عليه الشرع في قوله تعالى : [ ولا تحسبن الذين قتلوا في سبيل الله أمواتاً، بل أحياء عند ربهم، يرزقون، فرحين . . . إلخ ] وبقوله - صلى الله عليه وسلم - : [ أرواح الصالحين، في حواصل طيور خضر، معلقة تحت العرش ] . وبما ورد من الأخبار، بشعور الأرواح بالخيرات والصدقات وسؤال منكر ونكير، وعذاب القبر، وغيره، وكل ذلك يدل على البقاء . نعم قد دل مع ذلك على البعث والنشور بعده، وهو بعث البدن، وذلك ممكن، بردها إلى بدن، أى بدن كان، سواء كان من مادة البدن الأول أو من غيره، أو من مادة استؤنف خلقها، فإنه هو بنفسه لا ببدنه، إذ تتبدل عليه أجزاء البدن، من الصغر إلى الكبر، بالهزال والسمن، وتبدل الغذاء، ويختلف مزاجه مع ذلك، وهو ذلك الإنسان بعينه، فهذا مقدور الله تعالى، ويكون ذلك عوداً، لتلك النفس، فإنه كان قد تعذر عليها أنها تحظى بالآلام واللذات الجسمية، بفقد الآلة، وقد أعيدت إليها، آلة مثل الأولى، فكان ذلك عوداً محققاً
The objection: It is said, what do you say against one who chooses the last division and holds that the soul remains after death, and it is a self-subsistent substance (jawhar qā'im bi-nafsihī)? For that does not contradict the Law; rather, the Law indicates it in His statement (Exalted): 'Do not think that those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather they are alive with their Lord, being provided for, rejoicing...' and by his statement (peace be upon him): 'The spirits of the righteous are in the crops of green birds suspended beneath the Throne.' And by the reports that have come about the souls being aware of benefits and alms, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakīr, and the torment of the grave and other things—all of that indicates survival. Indeed, along with that, it indicates the resurrection and the rising after it, which is the raising of the body; and that is possible by returning it to a body, any body at all, whether from the material of the first body or from something else, or from matter whose creation is initiated—for the person is himself by his soul, not by his body, since the parts of his body change from childhood to adulthood, through emaciation and fatness, and change of food, and his temperament varies with that, yet he is that same human being. So this is within the power of Allah, and that would be a return of that soul, for it had been prevented from experiencing bodily pains and pleasures due to the loss of the instrument, and an instrument similar to the first has been restored to it, so that is a genuine return.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophical objector's case in favor of the third division (the soul returning to any body). The objector argues that the soul is a self-subsistent substance that survives death, citing Quranic verses (e.g., about martyrs being alive) and prophetic hadith (souls in green birds) as evidence for the soul's persistence after death. He then claims that resurrection is simply the soul's return to a body, which can be any body—the same material, different material, or newly created matter. The identity of the person lies in the soul, not the body, since the body changes throughout life. Therefore, resurrection is possible and constitutes a genuine return of the soul to a new body, enabling it to experience bodily pleasures and pains again. The objection ends by asserting this is within Allah's power and is a true return (ʿawd muḥaqqaq). This is the view that Ghazali will refute; the answer is not included in this page window.

Key Terms
نفس باقية (surviving soul)
جوهر قائم بنفسه (self-subsistent substance)
بعث (resurrection)
نشور (rising)
عود محقق (genuine return)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage represents Ghazali's own belief about the soul and resurrection.
Correction: This is the philosopher's objection that Ghazali refutes in the following pages. Ghazali does not hold that the soul is a self-subsistent substance that can be returned to any body.

Checkpoint
What does the objector identify as the basis for personal identity in resurrection?
A) The exact material of the first body.
B) The soul, not the body.
C) The specific organs of the body.
D) The moment of death.

Key Takeaway
The philosopher argues that the soul is a self-subsistent substance that persists after death, and resurrection is the return of this soul to any body, making personal identity independent of bodily continuity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your true identity is your soul and not your body, why do you spend so much effort beautifying your body while neglecting your soul? Honestly, does your daily routine reflect that you are a soul on a journey, or just a body chasing temporary pleasures? Let this question press you until you make a concrete change today.
?
The objector believes that any body will do for the soul's return. Does that make you feel that your current body is disposable? Or does it deepen your gratitude that Allah gave you this specific body as a trust? Do you treat your body as an amaanah, or do you use it carelessly? Write down one way you will honor that trust today.
?
The objector cites the verse about martyrs being alive with their Lord as evidence for the soul's survival. When you read that verse, do you truly feel the reality that those who die in Allah's way are alive? Does that belief change how you view your own death? Are you living in a way that you would be among those souls? If not, what is holding you back? Answer this not with words but with a change of direction.

Why the Reincarnation-like View is Invalid
Ghazali states that the view is identical to reincarnation and thus invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that a soul cannot attach to a new body after death, as this would lead to two souls in one body and is identical to the already-refuted doctrine of reincarnation.

Core Idea
Two souls cannot share one body; that is why reincarnation is impossible.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali confronts a view that allows a soul to take on a new body after death. He argues that such a view collapses into the already rejected doctrine of reincarnation (tanasukh). His reasoning is sharp and concise: if a body is prepared to receive a soul, then multiple souls could claim the same body, leading to an impossibility. Let us examine how he makes this case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to feel its rhythm, then the translation. Note the key terms: نفس (soul) and تناسخ (reincarnation).
2
Identify the core argument
Ghazali presents a conditional: if a soul could attach to any prepared body, then two souls would arrive at one body. This is impossible. Then he states this view is exactly reincarnation.
Focus on the phrase 'so two souls would arrive at one body'.
3
Connect to the refutation of reincarnation
Ghazali says the proof that invalidates reincarnation also invalidates this view. Ask yourself: what is that proof? It is the impossibility of two souls in one body.
This connects the specific refutation to a broader kalam principle.
4
Understand the implication
The view under discussion is not a separate theory; it is a form of reincarnation. Therefore, it is already ruled out by the established arguments against tanasukh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا التدبير ، ولا يمكن إعادة الإنسان ، وبدنه من خشب أو حديد ، بل لا يكون إنساناً إلا إذا انقسمت أعضاء بدنه إلى اللحم ، والعظم، والأخلاط، ومهما استعد البدن والمزاج ، لقبول نفس ، استحق من المبادئ الواهبة للنفوس ، حدوث نفس ، فيتوارد على البدن الواحد نفسان .
و بهذا بطل مذهب التناسخ، وهذا المذهب هو عين التناسخ ، فإنه رجع إلى اشتغال النفس ، بعد خلاصها من البدن ، بتدبير بدن آخر ، غير البدن الأول ، فالمسلك الذي يدل على بطلان التناسخ ، يدل على بطلان هذا المذهبه
This management, and it is not possible to restore a human being, his body being of wood or iron, rather he is not a human unless the parts of his body are divided into flesh, bone, and humors. And whenever the body and temperament are prepared to receive a soul, it deserves from the principles that bestow souls the occurrence of a soul, so two souls would arrive at one body. And by this the doctrine of reincarnation (tanāsukh) is invalidated, and this doctrine is exactly reincarnation, for it reverts to the soul's occupation, after its liberation from the body, with the management of another body other than the first body. So the path that indicates the invalidity of reincarnation indicates the invalidity of this doctrine.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a view that allows a soul to attach to a new body after death. Ghazali first describes the implausible consequence: if a soul could attach to any body (even one of wood or iron), then a human body requires specific parts (flesh, bone, humors). If any prepared body deserves a soul, then two souls would end up in one body, which is impossible. He then states that this view is exactly reincarnation (tanāsukh) and that the proof which refutes reincarnation also refutes this view. The argument is direct: the impossibility of two souls in one body and the equivalence to a doctrine already rejected.

Key Terms

تناسخ

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that a soul can attach to any new body after death, even one made of different materials.
Correction: Ghazali argues that this would lead to two souls in one body, which is impossible, and it is exactly the doctrine of reincarnation (tanasukh) that has been refuted.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument Ghazali uses to refute the view that a soul can attach to a new body after death?
A) The soul is not a substance.
B) This leads to two souls in one body and is identical to reincarnation.
C) The body must be made of the same material as the original.
D) The soul perishes with the body.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the view by showing it leads to the impossible scenario of two souls in one body, and that it is simply a form of the already-rejected doctrine of reincarnation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe in the resurrection of the body, but do you truly cherish your physical body as the unique vessel for your soul? Ghazali teaches that your body is not interchangeable—it must be flesh, bone, and humors. How does this truth challenge the way you treat your body today? What will you do this week to honor its divinely ordained role?
?
Ghazali equates the opposite view with reincarnation—a doctrine that allows the soul to 'start over' in another body. Do you sometimes live as if you can escape the consequences of your actions by imagining a fresh start? How does the Islamic insistence on one life, one body, and one resurrection press you to take full responsibility for your choices right now? What accountability do you feel standing before this truth?

The Objection and Initial Refutations
Ghazali presents the opponent's objection and his first two refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali refutes the opponent's scriptural argument for soul survival and the charges of infinite souls and reincarnation.

Core Idea
Scripture affirms soul survival, but resurrection is not reincarnation; divine power resolves the infinity problem.

The opponent argues that the soul's survival is scripturally proven and that resurrection is simply the soul joining any body. Ghazali begins his refutation by dismantling the claim that infinite souls require an eternal world, and then clarifies that the reincarnation label is irrelevant. This lesson presents these first two counterarguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The opponent quotes Quran and hadith to support soul survival, and defines resurrection as reunion with any body. Note how he uses scriptural evidence.
The opponent's argument is sophisticated, using both revelation and philosophical reasoning.
2
Examine Ghazali's reply on infinite souls
Ghazali says the infinity argument only holds if the world is eternal. For creationists, souls are finite and within divine power. Identify this key move.
3
Understand the reincarnation rebuttal
Ghazali argues that calling it reincarnation is just semantics. The Law commands belief in resurrection, so we accept it regardless of name.
This shows Ghazali's pragmatic approach: focus on the revealed truth, not labels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض ، أن يقال بم تنكرون على من يختار القسم الأخير ، ويرى أن النفس باقية بعد الموت ، وهى جوهر قائم بنفسه ، فإن ذلك لا يخالف الشرع بل دل عليه الشرع في قوله تعالى : [ ولا تحسبن الذين قتلوا في سبيل الله أمواتاً ، بل أحياء عند ربهم ، يرزقون ، فرحين . . . إلخ ] وبقوله - صلى الله عليه وسلم - : [ أرواح الصالحين ، في حواصل طيور خضر ، معلقة تحت العرش ] .
وبما ورد من الأخبار ، بشعور الأرواح بالخيرات والصدقات وسؤال منكر ونكير ، وعذاب القبر ، وغيره ، وكل ذلك يدل على البقاء . نعم قد دل مع ذلك على البعث والنشور بعده ، وهو بعث البدن ، وذلك ممكن ، بردها إلى بدن ، أى بدن كان ، سواء كان من مادة البدن الأول أو من غيره ، أو من مادة استؤنف خلقها ، فإنه هو بنفسه لا ببدنه ، إذ تتبدل عليه أجزاء البدن ، من الصغر إلى الكبر ، بالهزال والسمن ، وتبدل الغذاء ، ويختلف مزاجه مع ذلك ، وهو ذلك الإنسان بعينه ، فهذا مقدور الله تعالى ، ويكون ذلك عوداً ، لتلك النفس ، فإنه كان قد تعذر عليها أنه تحظى بالآلام واللذات الجسمية ، بفقد الآلة ، وقد أعيدت إليها ، آلة مثل الأولى ، فكان ذلك عوداً محققاً

وما ذكرتموه :
من
استحالة هذا بكون النفوس غير متناهية ، وكون المواد متناهية ، محال لا أصل له ، فإنه بناء على قدم العالم ، وتعاقب الأدوار على الدوام ، ومن لا يعتقد قدم العالم ، فالنفوس المفارقة للأبدان ، عنده متناهية ، وليست أكثر من المواد الموجودة ، وإن سلم أنها أكثر ، فالله تعالى قادر ، على الخلق واستئناف الاختراع ، وإنكاره إنكار لقدرة الله تعالى على الإحداث ، وقد سبق إبطاله في مسألة حدوث العالم . وأما إحالتكم الثانية ، بأن هذا تناسخ ، فلا مشاحة في الأسماء ، فما ورد الشرع به يجب تصديقه ، فليكن تناسخاً ، ونحن إنما ننكر التناسخ في هذا العالم ، وأما البعث فلا ننكره ، سمى تناسخاً ، أو لم يسم تناسخاً .
وقولكم : إن كل مزاج استعد لقبول نفس ، استحق حدوث نفس من المبادئ ، رجوع إلى أن حدوث النفوس، بالطبع لا بالإرادة ، وقد أبطلنا ذلك في مسألة حدوث العالم ، كيف ! ! ولا يبعد على مساق مذهبكم أيضاً ، أن يقال إنما يستحق حدوث نفس ، إذا لم تكن ثم نفس" موجودة" ، فتستأنف نفس
فيبقى أن يقال : فلم لم تتعلق بالأمزجة المستعدة في الأرحام قبل البعث والنشور ، بل فى عالمنا هذا
.
فيقال : لعل الأنفس المفارقة ، تستدعى نوعاً آخر من الاستعداد ، ولا يتم سببها إلا فى ذلك الوقت ، ولا بعد فى أن يفارق الاستعداد ، المشروط للنفس الكاملة المفارقة ، الاستعداد المشروط للنفس الحادثة ابتداء التي لم تستفد كمالا ، بتدبير البدن مدة ، والله تعالى أعلم ، بتلك الشروط ، وأسبابها ، وأوقات حضورها وقد ورد الشرع به ، وهو ممكن ، فيجب التصديق به
The objection: that it may be said: What do you deny to one who chooses the last division and holds that the soul endures after death, and it is a self-subsistent substance? For that does not contradict the Law; rather the Law indicates it in His saying (Exalted): 'Do not think those killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather they are alive with their Lord, provided for, rejoicing... etc.' and by his saying (peace be upon him): 'The souls of the righteous are in the crops of green birds suspended beneath the Throne.' And by what has come in reports of the souls' awareness of good deeds and charities, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, and the punishment of the grave, and other things; all that indicates survival. Yes, it has also indicated resurrection (ba‘th) and gathering (nushūr) after it, which is the raising of the body, and that is possible by returning them to a body, any body whatsoever, whether it is from the matter of the first body or from other than it, or from matter whose creation is begun anew. For he is identical by himself, not by his body, since the parts of the body change from childhood to old age, by emaciation and fatness, and the change of food, and his temperament varies with that, and he is that same human being. So this is within the power of Allah (Exalted), and that would be a return for that soul. For it had been prevented from obtaining bodily pains and pleasures due to the loss of the instrument, and an instrument similar to the first has been restored to it, so that is a verified return.
And what you mentioned of the impossibility of this by the souls being infinite and the materials finite is baseless and has no foundation; for it is built upon the eternity of the world and the succession of cycles perpetually. As for one who does not believe in the eternity of the world, the souls separate from bodies are finite in his view and are not more than the existing materials. And if it is conceded that they are more, then Allah (Exalted) is capable of creation and initiating invention; and denying that is a denial of the power of Allah (Exalted) to bring about new events, and its refutation has preceded in the issue of the origination of the world. As for your second objection, that this is reincarnation (tanāsukh), there is no quarrel about names. What the Law has brought must be believed; let it be reincarnation. For we only deny reincarnation in this world; as for the resurrection (ba‘th), we do not deny it, whether it is called reincarnation or not.
And your saying: Every temperament that is prepared to receive a soul deserves the occurrence of a soul from the principles is a return to the view that the occurrence of souls is by nature (tab‘) not by will (irāda). We have already refuted that in the issue of the origination of the world. How so! And it is not far in the course of your doctrine also to say that a soul deserves to occur only if there is no soul already existing, so a new soul would be initiated.
It remains to be said: Why did they not attach to the prepared temperaments in the wombs before the resurrection and gathering, but rather in this world of ours?
It is said: Perhaps the separate souls require another type of preparation, and their cause is not completed except at that time. There is no impossibility in that the preparation conditioned for the perfect separate soul is different from the preparation conditioned for the newly occurring soul that has not acquired perfection by managing the body for a time. And Allah (Exalted) knows best those conditions, their causes, and the times of their presence. And the Law has brought it, and it is possible, so it must be believed.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from an opponent and Ghazali's detailed refutation. First, the opponent argues that the soul's survival after death is clearly supported by scripture (the Quranic verse about martyrs and the hadith about souls of the righteous in green birds). The opponent also claims that resurrection is merely the reunion of the soul with any body, which is possible because personal identity is preserved by the soul, not the material body. Ghazali responds with several points: (1) The argument that souls are infinite and materials finite only holds if the world is eternal; for those who affirm creation, souls are finite and within divine power. (2) The charge that this is reincarnation is a semantic issue; what matters is that the Law affirms resurrection, and we only deny reincarnation in this world. (3) The opponent's suggestion that every prepared temperament deserves a soul leads to naturalism (that souls occur by nature rather than divine will), which was refuted earlier. (4) If souls could attach to any prepared body, why do they not attach to embryos in wombs before the resurrection? Ghazali answers that separate souls require a different kind of preparation, and only God knows the conditions. Since the Law affirms it and it is possible, it must be believed.

Key Terms
نفس
تناسخ
بعث
إرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that any reunion of soul with a body is reincarnation and therefore impossible.
Correction: Ghazali distinguishes worldly reincarnation from resurrection; the latter is revealed and possible by divine power.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does the argument that souls are infinite and materials finite not apply to those who believe in creation?
A) Because souls are created at the moment of resurrection.
B) Because the argument assumes the eternity of the world.
C) Because materials are also infinite.
D) Because souls are not substances.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali shows that scriptural evidence for soul survival does not entail reincarnation, and that supposed philosophical problems dissolve when one affirms creation and divine omnipotence.

?

Refuting Naturalism and the Timing of Resurrection
Ghazali continues his refutation by addressing naturalism and the timing of soul reunion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali refutes the opponent's claim that souls occur by nature, and why souls do not attach to bodies before the resurrection.

Core Idea
Souls are not produced by natural temperament but by divine will, and resurrection requires a special preparation known only to God.

The opponent further argues that if every prepared temperament deserves a soul, souls would occur by nature, not divine will. Ghazali responds by reaffirming the role of divine will and then addresses a remaining question: if souls can join any body, why do they not attach to embryos before the resurrection? This lesson covers these two arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the naturalism objection and reply
The opponent claims that temperament determines soul occurrence, implying naturalism. Ghazali reminds that this was refuted earlier in the discussion on the world's origination.
Note how Ghazali anchors this refutation in earlier arguments.
2
Address the timing problem
Why do souls wait until resurrection? Ghazali suggests that separate souls require a different type of preparation, and only God knows the conditions.
This shows Ghazali's reliance on divine wisdom and revelation.
3
Conclude with submission to revelation
Ghazali ends by stating that since the Law affirms resurrection and it is possible, we must believe it.

The objection: that it may be said: What do you deny to one who chooses the last division and holds that the soul endures after death, and it is a self-subsistent substance? For that does not contradict the Law; rather the Law indicates it in His saying (Exalted): 'Do not think those killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather they are alive with their Lord, provided for, rejoicing... etc.' and by his saying (peace be upon him): 'The souls of the righteous are in the crops of green birds suspended beneath the Throne.' And by what has come in reports of the souls' awareness of good deeds and charities, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, and the punishment of the grave, and other things; all that indicates survival. Yes, it has also indicated resurrection (ba‘th) and gathering (nushūr) after it, which is the raising of the body, and that is possible by returning them to a body, any body whatsoever, whether it is from the matter of the first body or from other than it, or from matter whose creation is begun anew. For he is identical by himself, not by his body, since the parts of the body change from childhood to old age, by emaciation and fatness, and the change of food, and his temperament varies with that, and he is that same human being. So this is within the power of Allah (Exalted), and that would be a return for that soul. For it had been prevented from obtaining bodily pains and pleasures due to the loss of the instrument, and an instrument similar to the first has been restored to it, so that is a verified return.
And what you mentioned of the impossibility of this by the souls being infinite and the materials finite is baseless and has no foundation; for it is built upon the eternity of the world and the succession of cycles perpetually. As for one who does not believe in the eternity of the world, the souls separate from bodies are finite in his view and are not more than the existing materials. And if it is conceded that they are more, then Allah (Exalted) is capable of creation and initiating invention; and denying that is a denial of the power of Allah (Exalted) to bring about new events, and its refutation has preceded in the issue of the origination of the world. As for your second objection, that this is reincarnation (tanāsukh), there is no quarrel about names. What the Law has brought must be believed; let it be reincarnation. For we only deny reincarnation in this world; as for the resurrection (ba‘th), we do not deny it, whether it is called reincarnation or not.
And your saying: Every temperament that is prepared to receive a soul deserves the occurrence of a soul from the principles is a return to the view that the occurrence of souls is by nature (tab‘) not by will (irāda). We have already refuted that in the issue of the origination of the world. How so! And it is not far in the course of your doctrine also to say that a soul deserves to occur only if there is no soul already existing, so a new soul would be initiated.
It remains to be said: Why did they not attach to the prepared temperaments in the wombs before the resurrection and gathering, but rather in this world of ours?
It is said: Perhaps the separate souls require another type of preparation, and their cause is not completed except at that time. There is no impossibility in that the preparation conditioned for the perfect separate soul is different from the preparation conditioned for the newly occurring soul that has not acquired perfection by managing the body for a time. And Allah (Exalted) knows best those conditions, their causes, and the times of their presence. And the Law has brought it, and it is possible, so it must be believed.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from an opponent and Ghazali's detailed refutation. First, the opponent argues that the soul's survival after death is clearly supported by scripture (the Quranic verse about martyrs and the hadith about souls of the righteous in green birds). The opponent also claims that resurrection is merely the reunion of the soul with any body, which is possible because personal identity is preserved by the soul, not the material body. Ghazali responds with several points: (1) The argument that souls are infinite and materials finite only holds if the world is eternal; for those who affirm creation, souls are finite and within divine power. (2) The charge that this is reincarnation is a semantic issue; what matters is that the Law affirms resurrection, and we only deny reincarnation in this world. (3) The opponent's suggestion that every prepared temperament deserves a soul leads to naturalism (that souls occur by nature rather than divine will), which was refuted earlier. (4) If souls could attach to any prepared body, why do they not attach to embryos in wombs before the resurrection? Ghazali answers that separate souls require a different kind of preparation, and only God knows the conditions. Since the Law affirms it and it is possible, it must be believed.

Key Terms
نفس
استعداد
إرادة
بعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why do resurrected souls not attach to prepared bodies in this world before the resurrection?
A) Because souls do not exist before resurrection.
B) Because the required preparation is different and only occurs at that time.
C) Because bodies in this world are not suitable.
D) Because God has not decreed it.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali reaffirms that resurrection is a unique event brought about by divine will, requiring conditions known only to God, and must be accepted on the basis of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You acknowledge that resurrection requires a special preparation known only to God. Are you living with that same dependence on divine will in every moment, or do you assume that your life follows natural laws alone? What would change if you truly lived as though everything—even your next breath—is by His will?
?
The passage says that separate souls require a different type of preparation for resurrection. Have you ever considered that your current life is precisely that preparation? What kind of soul are you becoming? If the conditions for resurrection are hidden in God's knowledge, do you trust His timing and wisdom for the outcome of your efforts?
?
Ghazali insists that since the Law affirms resurrection and it is possible, we must believe. Is your belief in resurrection merely intellectual assent, or does it move you to live as if you will be raised? Do you think about the resurrection often enough that it shapes your choices? If not, what needs to change today?

Refuting Infinite Souls and Transmigration Objections
Ghazali refutes two philosophical objections against bodily resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali refutes two philosophical objections against bodily resurrection: the infinite souls objection and the transmigration objection.

Core Idea
Ghazali defends bodily resurrection by dismantling philosophical assumptions and affirming God's power.

Ghazali here confronts two key objections raised by philosophers against the possibility of bodily resurrection. The first objection concerns infinite souls and finite bodies, while the second labels resurrection as transmigration (tanasukh). In this passage, he systematically shows that these objections rely on false premises and that resurrection is both possible and obligatory to believe.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Let the structure of Ghazali's argument become clear.
Notice that Ghazali addresses each objection in turn.
2
Identify the two objections
Look for the first objection about infinite souls and finite bodies, and the second objection that resurrection is transmigration.
3
Analyze Ghazali's refutation strategies
For the first objection, note how Ghazali points out it assumes the eternity of the world. For the second, observe his response about naming and the distinct status of resurrection.
Also pay attention to his criticism of natural necessity in soul-body attachment.
4
Connect to broader theological themes
Reflect on how Ghazali emphasizes God's absolute power and the authority of divine law over philosophical reasoning.
This passage ties into earlier discussions on the world's creation and causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكرتموه : من استحالة هذا بكون النفوس غير متناهية ، وكون المواد متناهية ، محال لا أصل له ، فإنه بناء على قدم العالم ، وتعاقب الأدوار على الدوام ، ومن لا يعتقد قدم العالم ، فالنفوس المفارقة للأبدان ، عنده متناهية ، وليست أكثر من المواد الموجودة ، وإن سلم أنها أكثر ، فالله تعالى قادر ، على الخلق واستئناف الاختراع ، وإنكاره إنكار لقدرة الله تعالى على الإحداث ، وقد سبق إبطاله في مسألة حدوث العالم . وأما إحالتكم الثانية ، بأن هذا تناسخ ، فلا مشاحة في الأسماء ، فما ورد الشرع به يجب تصديقه ، فليكن تناسخاً ، ونحن إنما ننكر التناسخ في هذا العالم ، وأما البعث فلا ننكره ، سمى تناسخاً ، أو لم يسم تناسخاً . وقولكم : إن كل مزاج استعد لقبول نفس ، استحق حدوث نفس من المبادئ ، رجوع إلى أن حدوث النفوس، بالطبع لا بالإرادة ، وقد أبطلنا ذلك في مسألة حدوث العالم ، كيف ! ! ولا يبعد على مساق مذهبكم أيضاً ، أن يقال إنما يستحق حدوث نفس ، إذا لم تكن ثم نفس موجودة ، فتستأنف نفس فيبقى أن يقال : فلم لم تتعلق بالأمزجة المستعدة في الأرحام قبل البعث والنشور ، بل في عالمنا هذا . فيقال : لعل الأنفس المفارقة ، تستدعى نوعاً آخر من الاستعداد ، ولا يتم سببها إلا في ذلك الوقت ، ولا بعد في أن يفارق الاستعداد ، المشروط للنفس الكاملة المفارقة ، الاستعداد المشروط للنفس الحادثة ابتداء التي لم تستفد كمالا ، بتدبير البدن مدة ، والله تعالى أعلم ، بتلك الشروط ، وأسبابها ، وأوقات حضورها وقد ورد الشرع به ، وهو ممكن ، فيجب التصديق به
And what you have mentioned: that this is impossible due to souls being infinite and bodies being finite, is baseless with no foundation. For it is built upon the eternity of the world and the succession of cycles perpetually. But whoever does not believe in the eternity of the world, then the souls that separate from bodies are finite in his view, and are not more than the existing bodies. And even if it is granted that they are more, then God Almighty is able to create and renew invention, and denying that is a denial of God's power to originate, and its refutation has already preceded in the question of the temporal creation of the world. As for your second objection, that this is transmigration (tanasukh), there is no quibbling over names. What the Law has brought must be believed. So let it be transmigration. We only deny transmigration in this world; as for the resurrection, we do not deny it, whether it is called transmigration or not. And your saying: Every temperament that is prepared to receive a soul deserves the occurrence of a soul from the principles, reverts to saying that the occurrence of souls is by nature not by will, and we have already refuted that in the question of the temporal creation of the world. How! And it is not unlikely according to your own doctrine that it be said: A soul deserves to occur only when there is no soul already existing, so a new soul is originated. Then it remains to be said: Why then did it not attach itself to the prepared temperaments in the wombs before the resurrection and the gathering, but rather in this world of ours? It is said: Perhaps the separate souls require another type of preparation, and its cause is not completed except at that time. There is no improbability that the preparation required for the perfect separate soul differs from the preparation required for the soul that originates initially and has not acquired perfection through managing the body for a period. And God Almighty knows best those conditions, their causes, and the times of their occurrence. The Law has brought it, and it is possible, so it must be believed.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two philosophical objections against bodily resurrection. Ghazali first addresses the claim that if souls are infinite and bodies finite, resurrection is impossible. He points out that this objection assumes the eternity of the world; for those who affirm temporal creation, souls are finite and not more than bodies. Even if souls were more, God's power to create new bodies is not limited—denying that is akin to denying God's creative power, already refuted earlier in the discussion of the world's origin. The second objection is that resurrection would be a form of transmigration (tanasukh). Ghazali replies that naming does not matter; the Law commands belief in resurrection, so even if it were called transmigration, it is accepted. What Muslims deny is transmigration in this world, not the afterlife. The philosophers also argued that a prepared temperament automatically deserves a soul, implying natural necessity. Ghazali counters that this reverts to naturalism, already refuted. He then poses a question: if souls arise only when no soul exists, why do they not attach to prepared bodies before resurrection? The answer is that separate souls for resurrection require a different kind of preparation, which only occurs at that time. Since the Law affirms this possibility, it must be believed.

Key Terms
تناسخ (tanasukh)
استعداد (preparation)
النفوس المفارقة (separate souls)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali accepts transmigration because he says 'so let it be transmigration'.
Correction: Ghazali distinguishes between worldly transmigration (denied) and resurrection (affirmed). He is not accepting transmigration as understood by philosophers; rather, he says even if it were called that, we still believe in resurrection because the Law commands it.

Checkpoint
Why does Ghazali reject the objection that souls are infinite and bodies finite?
A) Because he believes souls are created at death
B) Because the objection assumes the eternity of the world, which he rejects
C) Because bodies are also infinite
D) Because souls are material

Key Takeaway
Ghazali shows that philosophical objections to resurrection are based on flawed assumptions about the world's eternity and that belief in resurrection is obligatorily based on divine revelation, not human reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of your own death, do you genuinely expect a bodily resurrection, or do you subconsciously reduce it to a spiritual survival? What in your daily choices reveals your true belief?
?
Ghazali says that denying God's power to create new bodies is a denial of God's power. Where in your life do you limit God's power by assuming things are impossible for Him?
?
The philosophers argued that nature necessitates souls. Do you ever treat God's actions as if they are bound by natural laws? How does that affect your trust in specific answers to your duas?

The Necessary Composition of the Human Body
Ghazali defines the necessary composition and hierarchical dependency of the human body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali insists that a human body must have a specific composition of bones, flesh, and humors, not just any material.

Core Idea
A human body is defined by its specific composition, not by its material.

Ghazali begins by establishing that for a resurrected body to be truly human, it cannot be made of stone or precious gems. It must be shaped with a specific form and composed of bones, veins, flesh, cartilages, and humors. This introduces the concept that the resurrection body requires a particular physical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the full meaning.
Notice the list of materials that would not constitute a human body.
2
Identify the required composition
Ghazali lists the necessary components: bones, veins, flesh, cartilages, and humors. Highlight these terms.
3
Understand the hierarchical dependency
Trace the chain from simple parts (humors) to composite organs to the whole body. Note that each level depends on the previous.
This chain shows why arbitrary materials like stone cannot form a human body.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: Why does Ghazali emphasize this composition? He is countering the philosophers' objection that resurrection is impossible by showing that the body's structure is not arbitrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عقل هذا ؛ فالإنسان المبعوث المحشور ، لو كان بدنه من حجر ، أو ياقوت ، أو در ، أو تراب محض ، لم يكن إنساناً ، بل لا يتصور أن يكون إنساناً ، إلا أن يكون متشكلا ، بالشكل المخصوص ، مركباً من العظام ، والعروق ، واللحوم ، والغضاريف ، والأخلاط . والأجزاء المفردة ، تتقدم على المركبة ، فلا يكون البدن ، ما لم تكن الأعضاء ، ولا تكون الأعضاء المركبة ، ما لم تكن العظام ، واللحوم ، والعروق ، ولا تكون هذه المفردات ، ما لم تكن الأخلاط ، ولا تكون الأخلاط الأربعة ، ما لم تكن موادها ، من الغذاء ، ولا يكون الغذاء ، ما لم يكن حيوان أو نبات ؛ وهو اللحم والحبوب ، ولا يكون حيوان ونبات ، ما لم تكن العناصر الأربعة جميعاً ، ممتزجة بشرائط مخصوصة طويلة ، أكثر مما فصلنا جملتها . فإذن لا يمكن أن يتجدد بدن إنسان ، لترد النفس إليه ، إلا بهذه الأمور ، ولها أسباب كثيرة أفينقلب التراب إنساناً ، بأن يقال له كن ؟ أو بأن تمهد أسباب انقلابه ، في هذه الأدوار ؟! وأسبابه هى إلقاء النطفة المستخرجة ، من لباب بدن الإنسان ، في رحم ، حتى يستمد من دم الطمث ، ومن الغذاء مدة طويلة حتى يتخلق مضغة ، ثم علقة ، ثم جنيناً ، ثم طفلاً ، ثم شباباً ، ثم كهلاً ، ثم شيخاً .
And if this is understood, then the resurrected and gathered human being: if his body were of stone, or ruby, or pearl, or pure dust, he would not be a human being. Rather, he cannot be conceived as a human being unless he is shaped in the specific form, composed of bones, veins, flesh, cartilages, and humors. The simple parts precede the composite; the body does not exist unless the organs exist, and the composite organs do not exist unless the bones, flesh, and veins exist, and these simple parts do not exist unless the humors exist, and the four humors do not exist unless their materials from food exist, and food does not exist unless there is an animal or plant—that is, meat and grains—and animal and plant do not exist unless the four elements all are mixed with specific lengthy conditions, more than we have detailed in summary. Therefore, it is impossible for a human body to be renewed for the soul to return to it except through these matters, and they have many causes. So, does dust turn into a human being by saying to it 'Be'? Or by preparing the causes of its transformation through these stages? Its causes are the casting of the sperm extracted from the core of the human body into a womb, so that it draws from menstrual blood and from food for a long period until it becomes a clot, then a leech-like lump, then a fetus, then a child, then a youth, then an adult, then an old man.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the refutation of the philosophers' objection. Ghazali argues that for a body to be truly human, it must have a specific composition—bones, veins, flesh, cartilages, and humors—not just be made of stone or precious materials. He then outlines the necessary hierarchical dependency: simple parts (humors) must come before composite organs, and those require food from animals or plants, which in turn require the four elements mixed under specific conditions. This chain shows that the resurrection body cannot appear instantly from dust; it must go through the natural process of conception, gestation, and growth. Ghazali contrasts the miraculous command 'Be' with the actual long preparation through sperm, menstrual blood, nourishment, and developmental stages. The implication is that resurrection, though possible by God's power, follows a causal order that is not instantaneous but involves gradual transformation, just as the philosophers admitted for iron turning into cloth.

Key Terms
أخلاط (humors)
غضاريف (cartilages)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A human body can be made of any material as long as it has a human shape.
Correction: Ghazali insists that the body must be composed of specific biological parts (bones, flesh, humors) derived from food and elements, not just any substance like stone or ruby.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say is necessary for a body to be a human body?
It must be made of pure elements
It must be composed of bones, veins, flesh, cartilages, and humors
It must be created from nothing
It must be a single substance like stone

Key Takeaway
A human body is not any shaped matter; it requires a specific biological composition and a chain of material precursors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are alive and reading this because of a precise chain of materials and causes. If any link were missing, you would not exist. Have you ever truly felt your complete dependence on Allah for your very physical existence? Pause and thank Him for every bone, every vein, every morsel of food that sustains you.
?
Your body is not just a random collection of matter; it is a carefully composed gift that makes you human. Do you honor this gift by using your body in obedience to the One who designed it? What change will you make today to show gratitude for this specific composition?
?
Ghazali says that if your body were made of stone or ruby, you would not be human. Your identity is tied to this fragile, biological form. How does this shape your understanding of death and resurrection? Are you prepared to meet your Lord with the body He originally gave you?

The Gradual Process of Body Formation
Ghazali presents the impossibility of instantaneous resurrection and outlines the gradual developmental stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the resurrection body cannot appear instantly from dust but requires a gradual causal process.

Core Idea
God's command 'Be' is not the only way; resurrection follows a natural causal order.

Having established the necessary composition, Ghazali now argues that such a body cannot come about without a lengthy process involving sperm, womb, nourishment, and stages of development. He contrasts the instantaneous command 'Be' with the actual gradual transformation, using the philosophers' own causal principles against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the rhetorical question and the description of the developmental stages.
Notice the contrast between 'Be' and the long process.
2
Examine the rhetorical question
Ghazali asks: does dust turn into a human by the command 'Be' or by preparing causes? Consider the implication.
This highlights the difference between miraculous creation and natural causation.
3
Trace the developmental stages
List the stages from sperm to old age as described by Ghazali.
These stages mirror natural human development.
4
Understand the conclusion
Ghazali concludes that the resurrection body cannot be renewed except through these causes, implying it follows a natural process.
This refutes the philosophers' objection by showing that resurrection is not an abrupt impossibility but a gradual possibility.

Denial of Resurrection: Mere Improbability
Ghazali uses analogies to show denial of resurrection is based on ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses analogies to show that denial of resurrection is based on ignorance of divine power.

Core Idea
Absence of observation does not prove impossibility.

This passage presents a key argument from Imam Ghazali against those who reject bodily resurrection. Using the example of a magnet and embryonic development, Ghazali demonstrates that what seems impossible can be real. The lesson will explore his analogies and conclusion that denial rests on mere improbability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the flow of Ghazali's argument come through before interpreting.
2
Identify the two analogies
Find the magnet analogy and the embryonic development analogy. Notice how each shows that ignorance of a cause does not negate its existence.
3
Understand the tradition about resurrection rain
Ghazali cites a tradition about rain mixing with soil to suggest a method for resurrection. Consider how this reinforces his point that divine causes may be hidden.
4
Grasp the final conclusion
Ghazali ends by asking what basis the denier has except mere improbability. Reflect on how this challenges the assumption that the unobserved is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل لو لم ير إنسان المغناطيس ، وجذ به للحديد ، وحكى له ذلك ، لاستنكره ، وقال : لا يتصور جذب الحديد ، إلا بخيط يشد عليه ، ويجذب ، فإنه المشاهد فى الجذب ؛ حتى إذا شاهده تعجب منه ، وعلم أن علمه قاصر ، عن الإحاطة بعجائب القدرة وكذلك الملاحدة المنكرون للبعث والنشور ، إذا بعثوا من القبور ، ورأوا عجائب صنع الله تعالى ، فيهم ، ندموا ندامة لا تنفعهم ، ويتحسرون على جحودهم ، تحسراً لا يغنيهم ، ويقال لهم : « هذا الذي كنتم به تكذبون » كالذي يكذب بالخواص والأشياء الغريبة بل لو خلق إنسان عاقلا ابتداء ، وقيل له : إن هذه النطفة القذرة ، المتشابهة الأجزاء ، تنقسم أجزاؤها المتشابهة ، في رحم آدمية ، إلى أعضاء مختلفة، لحمية ، وعصبية ، وعظمية ، وعرقية ، وغضروفية ، وشحمية ، فيكون منها العين ، على سبع طبقات مختلفة فى المزاج ؛ واللسان ، والأسنان ، على ، في الرخاوة والصلابة ، مع تجاورهما ، وهلم جرا ، إلى البدائع التي في الفطرة - لكان إنكاره أشد من إنكار الملاحدة ، حيث قالوا : « كنا عظاماً نخرة . . . الآية » فليس يتفكر المنكر للبعث ، أنه من أين عرف انحصار أسباب الوجود ، شاهده ، ولم يبعد أن يكون فى إحياء الأبدان ، منهاج غير ما شاهده ، وقد ورد فى بعض الأخبار : أنه يغمر الأرض فى وقت البعث ، مطر ، قطراته تشبه النطف ، وتختلط بالتراب ، فأى بعد فى أن يكون فى الأسباب الإلهية أمر يشبه ذلك ، ونحن لا نطلع عليه ، ويقتضى ذلك انبعاث الأجساد ، و استعدادها لقبول النفوس المحشورة ، وهل لهذا الإنكار مستند ، إلا الاستبعاد المجرد .
But if a man had not seen the magnet and its attraction of iron, and it was described to him, he would deny it and say: 'It is inconceivable for iron to be attracted except by a string tied to it and pulled, for that is what is observed in attraction.' So that when he witnesses it, he marvels at it and knows that his knowledge is incapable of encompassing the wonders of [divine] power. Likewise, the heretics who deny the resurrection and the gathering, when they are raised from the graves and see the wonders of God's making among them, they will regret a regret that does not benefit them and grieve over their denial with a grief that does not avail them, and it will be said to them: 'This is what you used to deny.' Like one who denies strange properties and things. But if a rational person were created from the beginning and it was said to him: 'This filthy drop of semen, whose parts are similar, divides its similar parts in a woman's womb into different organs: fleshy, nervous, bony, venous, cartilaginous, and fatty, from which the eye is formed of seven layers differing in temperament; and the tongue and the teeth, [differing] in softness and hardness despite their proximity, and so on to the marvels of nature — his denial would be more severe than the denial of the heretics when they said: 'We were decayed bones...' So the denier of resurrection does not reflect: how did he know that the causes of existence are limited to what he has observed? It is not improbable that in the reviving of bodies there is a method other than what he has observed. It has been reported in some traditions that at the time of resurrection the earth will be covered by rain whose drops resemble sperm and mix with the soil. So what improbability is there that in the divine causes there is something like that, which we do not perceive, and that necessitates the resurrection of bodies and their preparedness to receive the gathered souls? And what basis does this denial have except mere improbability?
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny the resurrection based on unfamiliarity. Ghazali uses two analogies to show that the fact that we have not observed something does not mean it is impossible. First, he compares the denier to someone who has never seen a magnet attracting iron; that person would insist that attraction can only occur via a physical string. Only when he witnesses the magnet does he realize the limits of his knowledge. Similarly, the heretics who deny bodily resurrection will, upon witnessing it, regret their denial. Second, he imagines a person created ex nihilo who is told about embryonic development from a drop of semen into complex organs like the eye with seven different layers; such a person would vehemently deny it. Yet this process is a daily miracle. The point is that our empirical knowledge is limited. Ghazali then cites a tradition about rain at resurrection that mixes with soil, similar to sperm, to show that the divine method of reviving bodies may be analogous to the original creation. Therefore, the denier's only support is sheer improbability, not rational proof. This lesson emphasizes the principle that absence of observation does not prove impossibility, especially regarding divine power.

Key Terms
الملاحدة
البعث
النشور
الاستبعاد المجرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: What we haven't observed cannot happen.
Correction: Ghazali shows that divine power can bring about events beyond common experience; resurrection is not impossible just because we haven't seen it.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the only basis for the denier's rejection of resurrection?
A) Scriptural contradictions
B) Mere improbability
C) Lack of rational proof
D) Philosophical arguments

Key Takeaway
Denial of resurrection is based on mere improbability, not rational proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own life, in what area are you assuming that God cannot do something simply because you have never seen it happen? Will you now ask Him for that impossible thing, trusting that He can work beyond your observation?
?
Ghazali compares the denier to someone who sees a magnet for the first time. What 'magnet' have you been rejecting because it doesn't fit your worldview? Are you willing to have your assumptions shattered by God's power?
?
The analogy of embryonic development shows that what seems impossible to a mind created from nothing is actually a common miracle. How does this humble your sense of what is 'possible'? Will you yield your limited imagination to God's limitless creativity?

Objection: God's Unchanging Pattern
Objection: God's sunnah is unchangeable, so resurrection would recur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' objection that God's single fixed course of action precludes a unique resurrection.

Core Idea
God's sunnah never changes, so any event must recur eternally.

The philosophers argue that divine action follows one unalterable pattern, citing Quranic verses. If resurrection were possible, it would have to occur repeatedly, undermining the Islamic concept of a final, one-time resurrection. This lesson presents that objection in Ghazali's own formulation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the structure: objection, scriptural evidence, then logical consequence.
The passage uses 'فإن قيل' to indicate the objection begins.
2
Identify the key claim
The objector claims that divine action has a single fixed course (مجرى واحد). This is supported by two Quranic verses.
Verses: 'Our command is but one' and 'No change in God's sunnah'.
3
Understand the implication for resurrection
If resurrection were possible, it must fit into this unchanging pattern, meaning it would repeat cyclically, like procreation. This contradicts the belief in a single resurrection.
The objector uses the concept of 'طرد' (continuity) to force repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الفعل الإلهى له مجرى واحد مضروب ، لا يتغير ، ولذلك قال الله تعالى : [ وما أمرنا إلا واحدة كلمح البصر ] وقال تعالى : [ ولن تجد لسنة الله تبديلا ] ، وهذه الأسباب التي توهمتم إمكانها ، إن كانت ، فينبغي أن تطرد أيضاً ، وتتكرر إلى غير نهاية ، وأن يبقى هذا النظام الموجود في العالم ، من التولد والتوالد ، إلى غير نهاية . وبعد الاعتراف ، بالتكرر والدور ، فلا يبعد أن يختلف منهاج الأمور ، في كل ألف ألف سنة مثلا ، ولكن يكون ذلك التبدل أيضاً دائماً أبداً ، على سنن واحد ، فإن سنة الله تعالى ، لا تبديل فيها . وهذا إنما كان ، لأن الفعل الإلهى ، يصدر على المشيئة الإلهية ، والمشيئة الإلهية ، ليست متعددة الجهة ، حتى يختلف نظامها ، باختلاف جهاتها ، فيكون الصادر منها ، كيفما كان ، منتظماً انتظاماً ، يجمع الأول والآخر على نسق واحد ، كما تراه في سائر الأسباب والمسببات فإن جوزتم استمرار التوالد والتناسل ، بالطريق المشاهد الآن ، أو عود المنهاج ، ولو بعد زمان طويل ، على سبيل التكرار والدوام ، فقد رفعتم القيامة والآخرة ، وما دل عليه ظواهر الشرع ، إذ يلزم عليه أن يكون ، قد تقدم على وجودنا هذا ، البعث ، كرات ، وسيعود كرات ، وهكذا على الترتيب وإن قلتم إن السنة الإلهية بالكلية ، تتبدل إلى جنس آخر ، ولا تعود قط هذه السنة ، وتنقسم مدة هذا الإمكان ، إلى ثلاثة أقسام : قسم قبل خلق العالم ، إذ كان الله تعالى ولا عالم . بعد خلقه على هذا الوجه وقسم قسم به الاختتام ، وهو المنهاج البعثى بطل الاتساق والانتظام ، وحصل التبديل لسنة الله تعالى ، وهو محال
For it is said: Divine action has a single fixed course that does not change. For that reason God said: 'Our command is but one, like the twinkling of an eye' and 'You will not find any change in God's sunnah.' So these causes that you imagine possible, if they exist, should also be continuous and repeated ad infinitum, and this existing system in the world of generation and procreation should remain ad infinitum. And after conceding repetition and cycles, it is not improbable that the course of things should vary, for example every hundred thousand years, but that change would also be everlasting, in a single pattern, for there is no change in God's sunnah. This is because divine action proceeds from the divine will, and the divine will is not multiple in aspect such that its system would differ due to different aspects. Rather, whatever issues from it is systematically ordered, combining the first and the last in a single order, as you see in all causes and effects. For if you allow the continuation of procreation and reproduction by the presently observed method, or the return of the course even after a long time, on a recurring and perpetual basis, then you have undermined the resurrection and the Hereafter and what the apparent meanings of the Law indicate, for it would entail that before our current existence there was resurrection multiple times, and it will return multiple times, and so on in sequence. And if you say that the divine sunnah completely changes to another kind, and this sunnah never returns at all, and the duration of this possibility is divided into three divisions: a division before the creation of the world, when God existed and there was no world; a division after its creation in this manner; and a division that is the conclusion, which is the resurrection course — then consistency and order would be broken, and a change in God's sunnah would occur, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the consistency of God's actions. The objector argues that God's action follows a single unchangeable pattern, citing Quranic verses about His command being 'one' and His sunnah having no change. Therefore, if resurrection were possible, it would imply repetition of the pattern, meaning that resurrection should occur repeatedly, and the world would continue in cycles of procreation. The objector also argues that even if the pattern were to change occasionally, it would still follow a consistent rule of change, so resurrection would be part of a recurring cycle, which conflicts with religious teachings that resurrection is a one-time event. Ghazali, through the objector, then presents a further possibility: one might claim that the divine sunnah changes entirely to a different kind, with three divisions: before creation (God alone), after creation in this pattern, and the final resurrection pattern. But that would break the consistency and order, and changing the sunnah is impossible. The passage ultimately defends the orthodox view that resurrection is a unique, non-recurring event that does not violate the consistency of divine action because God's will is singular and the pattern remains consistent in the sense that it encompasses all events in a single divine decree.

Key Terms
الفعل الإلهى (divine action)
المجرى (course)
سنة الله (God's sunnah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's sunnah changing means He cannot perform any unique act.
Correction: This lesson shows the objection that sunnah's immutability forces repetition of events; it does not permit a one-time event.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's main claim about divine action?
A) It changes over time
B) It has a single fixed course that does not change
C) It is unpredictable
D) It only applies to procreation

Key Takeaway
The objection asserts that because God's sunnah never changes, resurrection would have to recur eternally, contradicting Islamic teaching of a single final event.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever let the regularity of nature make you forget that God can act uniquely in your life? When have you assumed that God's past ways with you must repeat, rather than expecting Him to do something utterly new?
?
The philosophers argued that resurrection cannot happen because God's pattern never changes. Are there areas of your life where you have limited God by your expectations of how He 'always' works? What would it mean to trust in His absolute freedom even when it seems to break the pattern?
?
In this passage, the objectors treat God's consistency as a constraint. How does your heart view God's steadfastness? As a comforting promise that He will abide by His word, or as a limitation that makes you doubt He can intervene in unexpected ways? Commit to one specific area where you will pray for God to act beyond your expectations.

Response: Resurrection Is Unique and Consistent
Response: Evaluating scenarios to defend resurrection's uniqueness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's response that resurrection does not break God's pattern because divine will is singular and can produce unique events without repetition.

Core Idea
A single divine will can create a unique event without recurring.

After presenting the objection, Ghazali now addresses the implications. If we accept continuous procreation, that would negate resurrection as a final event. Alternatively, if we claim the divine sunnah completely changes to a resurrection course, that would be a change in God's sunnah, which is impossible. This lesson shows how Ghazali navigates these points.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two scenarios: continuous procreation or complete change of sunnah.
The passage begins with 'فإن جوزتم' indicating a conditional.
2
Analyze the first scenario
If procreation continues forever, resurrection would be just another cycle, undermining the unique final resurrection.
This is the consequence of the objector's logic.
3
Analyze the second scenario
If the sunnah completely changes to a resurrection course, that would be a change in God's sunnah, which is impossible according to the objector's own premise.
The objector's argument is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?

The Immortality of the Soul: Two Philosophical Views
Ghazali reports the views of Aristotle, Ibn Sina, and Plato on the soul's survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contrasting views of Aristotle/Ibn Sina and Plato on the survival of human souls and the nature of Ghazali's critique.

Core Idea
Two philosophies, one core question: Are souls many or one after death?

Before engaging in his own arguments, Ghazali presents the philosophical views he intends to critique. Here he outlines two opposing positions: the Aristotelian-Avicennan view of individual immortal souls and the Platonic view of a single soul that divides and reunites. Understanding these views is essential to following the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the two views presented. Observe that the passage ends with a mention of an objection to Plato.
The passage is reporting, not arguing. Ghazali is setting up the positions for critique.
2
Identify the two views
Distinguish the view of Aristotle and Ibn Sina from that of Plato. Aristotle/Ibn Sina hold souls are many, infinite, and immortal. Plato holds the soul is one, eternal, but divides in bodies.
Key terms: 'باقية' (lasting), 'غير فانية' (not perishing), 'واحدة قديمة' (one eternal).
3
Consider the objection
Notice that Ghazali mentions an objection to Plato's view. Think about why a single soul dividing might be problematic—it may contradict the individuality of human experience.
This objection will be elaborated in subsequent lessons.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why these views matter for Islamic theology. The debate touches on resurrection, accountability, and the nature of the self.
This lesson is foundational for understanding Ghazali's critique of philosophy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأى أرسطو وابن سينا أن نفوس الآدميين باقية غير فانية ، وهي غير متناهية. رأى أفلاطون أن النفس واحدة قديمة وإنما تنقسم في الأبدان ، فإذا فارقتها عادت إلى أصلها واتحدت. الاعتراض على رأى أفلاطون
The view of Aristotle and Ibn Sina is that the souls of humans are lasting, not perishing, and they are infinite. The view of Plato is that the soul is one and eternal, and it only divides in bodies; when it leaves them it returns to its origin and unites. The objection to Plato's view.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage presents two opposing philosophical views on the nature and destiny of human souls. Aristotle and Ibn Sina hold that each human soul is individually immortal and infinite in number. Plato holds that there is a single eternal soul that divides among bodies and re-unites after death. The mention of an objection to Plato's view indicates that Ghazali will critique it, likely challenging the notion of a single soul.

Key Terms
نفس
باقية
فانية
متناهية
قديمة
انقسام
اتحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ghazali is presenting these views as correct or that he agrees with them.
Correction: Ghazali is merely reporting the philosophical positions in order to critique them from an Islamic standpoint. He does not endorse either view.

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the view of Aristotle/Ibn Sina and that of Plato regarding human souls?
A) Aristotle and Ibn Sina say souls are many and immortal; Plato says the soul is one and divides
B) Aristotle and Ibn Sina say souls are eternal; Plato says they are created
C) Aristotle and Ibn Sina say souls perish; Plato says they are immortal
D) Aristotle and Ibn Sina say souls are divisible; Plato says they are indivisible

Key Takeaway
Aristotle and Ibn Sina view human souls as individually immortal and many, while Plato views the soul as a single eternal entity that divides in bodies and reunites after death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Does your life reflect that your soul is uniquely accountable before Allah, or do you sometimes act as if your deeds don't matter because you'll just merge into a cosmic whole? How does knowing that Islam teaches individual souls change how you view your repentance and prayer?
?
If you believed your soul would lose its identity after death (like Plato's view), would you still feel the urgency to correct your character and seek forgiveness? What does your answer reveal about your actual belief?
?
The passage presents philosophies that deny personal immortality in the Islamic sense. Are you more influenced by cultural ideas that downplay individual accountability? Ask yourself: Do I truly live as if my soul will meet Allah alone on Judgment Day, or do I lean on excuses that blur this truth?

The Possibility of the Human Soul
Ghazali applies possibility principle to three soul views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali applies the principle of possibility to the human soul and why the objection about possibility requiring a material subject does not apply even to an immaterial soul.

Core Idea
The possibility of an immaterial soul is a relation to matter, not a property in a subject.

Ghazali now turns to a specific case: the human soul. Philosophers differ on whether the soul is eternal or created, material or immaterial. Here, he tests each view against the criterion established earlier—that possibility is always relational, not an inherent quality. Even Ibn Sina's view of a created, immaterial soul fits this framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Ghazali's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the three positions he lists.
2
Identify the three positions on the soul
The passage presents three different views: soul eternal, soul impressed in matter, soul created and immaterial. For each, Ghazali reinterprets 'possibility' as a relation.
What does 'possibility' mean in each case?
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ghazali concludes 'nothing follows' for any of these views. Ask yourself why this means the earlier refutation stands.
This shows the principle is robust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و إن نفوس الآدميين عند ابن سينا حادثة ومجردة عن المادة ، فبماذا قام إمكانها قبل وجودها ؟. وأما النفس فقد قيل : إنها قديمة ، وإمكانها معناه : إمكان تعلقها بالأبدان وقيل : إنها منطبعة فى مادة ، تابعة للمزاج ، فتكون في مادة ، وإمكانها مضاف إلى مادتها ومن قال : إنها حادثة ومجردة عن المادة ، فإمكانها معناه : أن المادة ممكن لها أن تدبرها نفس ناطقة لا فلم يلزم شيء مما قيل سابقاً
And the souls of humans, according to Ibn Sīnā, are temporally originated and abstract from matter; so in what did their possibility subsist before their existence? And as for the soul, it has been said: it is eternal, and its possibility means the possibility of its attachment to bodies. And it has been said: it is impressed in matter, following the temperament, so it is in matter, and its possibility is attributed to its matter. And whoever says it is temporally originated and abstract from matter, its possibility means that matter is possible for it to be governed by a rational soul. So nothing of what was said previously follows.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a short application of the previous principle to the specific case of the human soul (nafs). Ghazali first poses the challenge: if the soul is, according to Ibn Sīnā, temporally originated (ḥāditha) and immaterial (mujarrada ʿan al-mādda), then what did its possibility subsist in before its existence? He then reviews three different positions on the soul. The first: the soul is eternal (qadīma), so its possibility means the possibility of its attachment (taʿalluq) to bodies. The second: the soul is impressed (munṭabiʿa) in matter, following the temperament (mizāj), so its possibility is attributed to its matter. The third: the soul is temporally originated and immaterial, so its possibility means that matter is possible for it to be governed by a rational soul (nafs nāṭiqa). In all these cases, Ghazali concludes that 'nothing of what was said previously'—meaning the objections that possibility requires a material subject—necessarily follows. That is, even for an immaterial soul, the possibility is not a property inhering in a subject; it is a relational judgment (e.g., matter's capacity to be governed). Thus the earlier refutation stands.

Key Terms
النفوس
ابن سينا
حادثة
مجردة عن المادة
مطبعة في المادة
نفس ناطقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That an immaterial soul's possibility must inhere in some substance or subject.
Correction: Ghazali shows that possibility for an immaterial soul is a relational judgment: matter's capacity to be governed by a rational soul. No inherent property is needed.

Checkpoint

B) The possibility of matter being governed by a rational soul
C) The possibility of the soul's attachment to bodies
D) The soul's possibility is the same as the body's possibility

Key Takeaway
The possibility of the human soul, even if immaterial, is always a relational judgment about matter, never an inherent quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul's possibility before existence was simply that your matter could be governed by a rational soul, then your entire existence is a gift of relation. Have you truly acknowledged that dependence today, or do you live as if your soul is self-sufficient?

The soul's possibility is tied to its attachment to the body. In your daily life, is your soul governing your body, or is it being overwhelmed by bodily desires? What one change can you make right now to restore that governance?
?
The possibility of the soul is not an inherent quality but a relation to matter. Does this perspective change how you view your own identity? Are you more than just a soul, or are you a soul-body relation? How does that affect your accountability before Allah?

The Limits of Reason on Bodily Resurrection
Ghazali refutes the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection based on revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali insists that bodily resurrection and other eschatological details are known through divine revelation, not through unaided human reason.

Core Idea
Revelation, not reason, is the source of our knowledge of the afterlife.

This lesson examines Ghazali's decisive critique of the philosophers' claim that bodily resurrection is only a metaphor for spiritual realities. He affirms that while spiritual pleasures exist, the specific promises of Paradise, Hell, and bodily resurrection are known only through the revealed law (sharʿ). The philosophers' error is not in affirming spiritual rewards, but in denying the physical and in relying on reason alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Ghazali structures his response: first stating the philosophers' view, then declaring it contrary to Muslim belief, then clarifying his own position.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يفهم المعاد إلا ببقاء النفس' — the Return is understood only through the soul's survival.
2
Identify Ghazali's two-fold response
Ghazali does two things: (1) he rejects the philosophers' metaphorical interpretation of bodily resurrection, and (2) he clarifies that he does accept spiritual pleasures and the soul's survival, but through revelation.
This is a common rhetorical move: first refute, then clarify to avoid misunderstanding.
3
Understand the role of revelation
Ghazali says he knows about the afterlife by the revealed law (al-sharʿ). He does not deny reason but limits its scope for details like bodily resurrection.
This sets the stage for the Ashʿarī principle that matters of the unseen require scriptural authority.
4
Reflect on the central disagreement
The core disagreement is epistemological: can reason alone tell us about bodily resurrection? Ghazali says no. The philosophers say yes (by allegorizing). This lesson highlights that debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
28 - مسألة فى إبطال إنكارهم لبعث الأجساد، ورد الأرواح إلى الأبدان، ووجود النار الجسمانية، ووجود الجنة والحور العين، وسائر ما وعد به الناس؛ وقولهم إن كل ذلك أمثلة ضربت لعوام الخلق لتفهيم ثواب وعقاب روحانيين، هما أعلى رتبة من الجسمانيين. قال الغزالى : وهذا مخالف لاعتقاد المسلمين كافة. ثم قال : فلنقدم تفهيم مذهبهم أولا، ثم نعترض على ما يخالف الإسلام منه. ... فانظر مذهبهم. قال الغزالي : إننا لا ننكر أن في الآخرة أنواعاً من اللذات أعظم من المحسوسات، ولا ننكر بقاء النفس عند مفارقة البدن، ولكننا عرفنا ذلك بالشرع؛ إذ قد ورد بالمعاد ولا يفهم المعاد إلا ببقاء النفس، وإنما أنكرنا عليهم دعواهم معرفة ذلك بمجرد العقل.
Issue 28: On refuting their denial of the resurrection of bodies, the return of spirits to bodies, and the existence of the bodily fire, and the existence of Paradise and the wide-eyed maidens (ḥūr al-ʿayn), and all that has been promised to people; and their statement that all of that are examples (amthila) struck for the common people to make them understand a spiritual reward and punishment which are of a higher rank than the bodily ones. Al-Ghazālī said: This contradicts the belief of all Muslims. Then he said: Let us first present their doctrine, then we will object to what contradicts Islam from it. ... So consider their doctrine. Al-Ghazālī said: We do not deny that in the Hereafter there are types of pleasures greater than the sensual ones, and we do not deny the survival of the soul upon separation from the body, but we know that by the revealed law (al-sharʿ); for the Return (al-maʿād) has come [in revelation] and the Return is not understood except by the survival of the soul. We only deny their claim to know that by mere intellect (al-ʿaql).
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage introduces Issue 28, where Ghazali refutes the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection and their interpretation of eschatological rewards as mere metaphors for spiritual pleasures. He declares that their view contradicts the consensus of Muslims. He outlines his method: first present the philosophers' doctrine, then critique what opposes Islam. He clarifies that he does not reject the existence of higher spiritual pleasures or the survival of the soul; rather, he affirms these through revelation (sharʿ). The only point of contention is the philosophers' claim to know these realities through reason alone, which Ghazali rejects. This sets the stage for the detailed refutation to follow.

ثواب وعقاب روحانيين
شرع

Misconception: Ghazali rejects all spiritual pleasures and the soul's survival.
Correction: Ghazali affirms spiritual pleasures and the soul's survival, but insists they are known through revelation, not reason.

Checkpoint

B) They claim to know about the afterlife by reason alone.
C) They reject all pleasures of the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali affirms bodily resurrection and eschatological details as revealed truths, rejecting the philosophers' rationalist allegorization while still acknowledging higher spiritual pleasures.
